Plugins are compiled to WebAssembly and executed in a wasmi runtime sandbox. This means plugins can extend or replace Zellij's UI elements (status bar, tab bar, pane decorations) without risking the stability of the core application.\n\n## Development & Requirements\n\nZellij 0.41 introduces non-colliding keybindings and a new plugin manager, requiring Rustc 1.89+ and Cargo 2.1+ for plugin development. To ensure compatibility, use the wasm32-wasi target (0.1.0) in Cargo.toml for Rust-based plugins and ZIP files for non-Rust plugins.\n\n## Plugin SDK API\n\nThe Plugin SDK (zellij-tile/) exposes a clean Rust API. Plugin authors implement the ZellijPlugin trait with three key methods: load() (initialization), update() (event handling), and render() (drawing to the pane). The register_plugin! macro handles all the WASM ABI boilerplate, serializing/deserializing events and configuration via Protobuf. For long-running tasks, the ZellijWorker trait provides a background worker pattern that communicates with the main plugin instance via message passing.\n\n## Security & Performance\n\nThe plugin system uses WebAssembly (WASM), which means that it is fast, crash-proof, and works identically across any computer. The major design goals include not requiring terminal emulators to understand image formats, allowing graphics to be drawn at individual pixel positions, and enabling graphics to integrate with text with alpha blending.\n\n## Kittens Framework\n\nKitty has a framework for creating subprograms called kittens, with commands for all kittens prefixed with \"kitty +kitten\". Kittens are lightweight Python scripts invoked via kitty @ RPC, enabling custom layouts, inline images via the Kitty Graphics Protocol, and seamless tab management.\n\n## API and Embedding\n\nKitty provides powerful interfaces such as Control kitty from scripts and Custom kittens that allow it to be integrated with other tools seamlessly. A Block groups commands and outputs into one atomic unit.\n\n## Discrete Architecture\n\nWarp separates commands into blocks, and each block consists of three grids: one for the prompt, one for the command input, and one for the command output. This architectural design creates a structured approach to terminal output rather than treating it as a continuous stream.\n\n## Impact on Terminal Structure\n\nBlocks transform the terminal from a continuous scroll into a structured document. Warp fundamentally changes this by grouping each command and its output into discrete, selectable blocks -- making it trivial to copy results, scroll through long output, or share a specific command's result with a teammate.\n\n## Practical Features Enabled by Block Architecture\n\nThe discrete block architecture enables several capabilities:\n- Every block is an independent object that can be searched, filtered, or shared.\n- Blocks can visually flag failed commands based on exit codes, allowing developers to quickly scan their history for issues.\n- Because the terminal \"understands\" where a command's output ends, it can offer smart actions like \"copy output\" or \"explain error\" directly within the block's footer.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"4bc79ea9-2aa9-4c59-800f-b37ef462ea49","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:44:24.481Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"7500126a-4f58-44d9-a12b-cab05bec0c08","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

Mitchell Hashimoto states: \"a zero-dependency library that provides an API for parsing terminal sequences and maintaining terminal state.\"\n\nThe Zig API is currently available for testing through a merged pull request that \"includes a minimal example program.\" However, the C API is not yet ready but is actively being developed.\n\n## Key Components\n\n### libghostty-vt (Terminal VT Parsing)\nThis foundational library handles:\n- Parsing terminal escape sequences\n- Maintaining cursor position, styles, and text wrapping state\n- Zero dependencies (not even libc required)\n- SIMD-optimized parsing inherited from Ghostty\n- Support for Kitty Graphics Protocol and Tmux Control Mode\n\n### Planned Future Libraries\nThe roadmap includes additional `libghostty-<x>` modules for:\n- Input handling and keyboard encoding\n- GPU rendering (OpenGL/Metal surface support)\n- GTK widgets and Swift frameworks for terminal views\n\n## Platform Support\n\nInitial targets:\n- macOS and Linux\n- x86_64 and aarch64 architectures\n\nPlanned expansion:\n- Windows\n- Embedded devices\n- Web via WebAssembly\n\n## API Design\n\nThe library exposes \"a C API so feature-rich, correct, and fast terminal functionality can be embedded by any application anywhere.\" Development uses a \"clean slate approach\" rather than repurposing Ghostty's internal-only C API.\n\n## Quality Assurance\n\nThe core logic is \"extremely stable and proven in the real world\" through extensive Ghostty usage, including SIMD optimization, Unicode support, fuzzing, and Valgrind testing.\n\n## Timeline\n\nMitchell Hashimoto aims to \"ship a tagged version of libghostty-vt within the next 6 months,\" pending readiness, with versioning independent from the Ghostty The project uses Raylib for windowing and 2D graphics rendering, deliberately avoiding GPU-accelerated approaches to demonstrate libghostty's flexibility across different contexts.\n\n## Core Technology: libghostty-vt\n\nThe project leverages **libghostty-vt**, described as \"a zero-dependency library (not even libc) that handles VT sequence parsing, terminal state management\" and renderer coordination. This library extracts core terminal logic directly from Ghostty, the primary terminal emulator.\n\nThe library provides substantial real-world benefits inherited from Ghostty's proven implementation:\n- SIMD-optimized parsing\n- Robust Unicode support\n- Highly optimized memory usage\n- Extensively fuzzed and tested codebase\n\n## Demonstrated Capabilities\n\nDespite its minimalist approach, Ghostling displays comprehensive terminal features:\n\n**Text & Color Support:**\n- 24-bit color and 256-color palette rendering\n- Bold, italic, and inverse text styling\n- Unicode and multi-codepoint grapheme handling\n\n**Interaction Features:**\n- Keyboard input with modifier support (Shift, Ctrl, Alt, Super)\n- Kitty keyboard protocol support\n- Multiple mouse tracking modes (X10, normal, button, any-event)\n- Scrollbar with drag-to-scroll functionality\n- Focus reporting capability\n\n**Dynamic Behavior:**\n- Terminal resize with text reflow\n\n## Significance for Embedding Ghostty\n\nGhostling demonstrates that libghostty enables embedding production-quality terminal emulation without requiring specific rendering frameworks. {"parentUuid":"21383bae-6fc7-4910-b777-cf49e192c804","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3cc0f97d-a1f5-45ea-9b1f-f2c4ba2c0638","agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01WfWmhN73XPB5og9MmWAeXX","type":"tool_result","content":"# ghostty-web: Technical Overview\n\n## What It Is\n\nghostty-web is a browser-based terminal emulator that brings Ghostty's rendering engine to the web. It's distributed as an npm package with xterm.js API compatibility, allowing developers to migrate from xterm by simply changing their import statement from `@xterm/xterm` to `ghostty-web`.\n\n## Core Architecture\n\nThe project compiles Ghostty's terminal parser into WebAssembly, creating what amounts to the same emulation engine that powers the native desktop application. Rather than reimplementing VT100 sequences in JavaScript, ghostty-web reuses battle-tested native code through compilation.\n\n**Bundle characteristics:**\n- Approximately 400KB WASM bundle\n- Zero runtime dependencies\n- 99.2% TypeScript codebase\n\n## How It Works\n\nThe implementation requires patching Ghostty's source to expose additional functionality for web use. The build process:\n\n1. Takes the Ghostty source (included as a git submodule)\n2. Applies a minimal patch to enable WASM API exposure\n3. Compiles via Zig toolchain\n4. Bundles through Bun package manager\n\nPer the documentation, the patch layer remains \"very minimal\" due to foundational work by the Ghostty team on `libghostty`.\n\n## xterm.js Compatibility\n\nghostty-web implements the xterm.js API surface, enabling drop-in replacement scenarios. Core methods include:\n\n- `Terminal()` constructor with theme and font configuration\n- `.open()` to mount in DOM\n- `.onData()` callback for input handling\n- `.write()` for rendering output\n\nA practical example shows WebSocket integration:\n```javascript\nterm.onData((data) => websocket.send(data));\nwebsocket.onmessage = (e) => term.write(e.data);\n```\n\n## Advantages Over xterm.js\n\nThe comparison highlights specific gaps xterm.js fails to address:\n\n| Feature | xterm.js | ghostty-web |\n|---------|----------|------------|\n| Complex script rendering (Devanagari, Arabic) | Issues present | Proper grapheme handling |\n| XTPUSHSGR/XTPOPSGR sequences | Unsupported | Full support |\n\nSince xterm.js hand-codes terminal logic in JavaScript, every edge case and Unicode quirk requires individual implementation. Ghostty's approach leverages production-tested native code.\n\n## Current Status\n\n- **Latest release:** v0.4.0 (December 9, 2025)\n- **Repository stats:** 2.3k stars, 113 commits, 22 open issues\n- **Live demo:** Available at ghostty.ondis.co (ephemeral VM)\n- **Local testing:** `npx @ghostty-web/demo@next` launches an HTTP server with shell access on localhost:8080 (Linux/macOS optimized)\n\n## Known Limitations\n\nThe development notes indicate this represents an interim approach. Mitchell Hashimoto (Ghostty's author) is developing a native WASM distribution (`libghostty`). Once available, ghostty-web will consume that instead of patching source code directly, with the xterm.js-compatible API layer continuing as before.\n\nThe project explicitly acknowledges that current patches are expected to diminish once native WASM support matures."}]},"uuid":"a280761c-1f03-49f3-9cfc-8a783b8c1fac","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:45:10.494Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"21383bae-6fc7-4910-b777-cf49e192c804","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

{"parentUuid":"be58f3cf-d814-40d6-b294-f7927fd0030d","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3cc0f97d-a1f5-45ea-9b1f-f2c4ba2c0638","agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XZ1F7qRwem2cR7P4KKXkma","type":"tool_result","content":"# Zellij Web Client: Technical Architecture & Capabilities\n\n## Core Architecture\n\nZellij implements a **single web-server-per-machine model** that serves multiple terminal sessions. The web server acts as a translation layer, converting browser WebSocket communications into IPC (Inter-Process Communication) channels that connect to Zellij's background server processes.\n\nThe design enables browser clients to appear as regular users within terminal sessions, \"blurring the distinction between the two user interfaces.\"\n\n## Key Capabilities\n\n**Session Management via URLs:**\nSessions are accessible through intuitive URLs (e.g., `https://127.0.0.1/backend-code`). The system supports three scenarios:\n- Attaching to running sessions\n- Resurrecting previous sessions from serialized metadata\n- Creating new sessions on-demand\n\nThis creates \"a terminal a URL bar: we can bookmark entire sessions (eg. prod, frontend, backend).\"\n\n**Bi-directional Communication:**\nTwo separate WebSocket channels handle:\n- **Terminal channel**: STDOUT (ANSI rendering instructions) and STDIN (keypresses, mouse events)\n- **Control subchannel**: Window resizes, configuration changes, and session-switch instructions\n\nSeparation prevents blocking and optimizes performance for high-throughput STDOUT data.\n\n## Technical Stack\n\n**Server-side (Rust):**\n- **Framework**: Axum web server with declarative routing\n- **Runtime**: Tokio for async I/O\n- **Security**: Rustls for HTTPS (avoiding OpenSSL complexity)\n- **Assets**: `include_dir!` macro bundles static files within the executable\n- **Daemonization**: Custom `daemonize` crate integration using Unix pipes for error reporting between parent/child processes\n\n**Client-side:**\n- **Terminal**: xterm.js library (battle-tested, used in VSCode)\n- **Language**: Vanilla JavaScript (no build step)\n- **Custom integrations**: Mouse AnyEvent tracking via browser mousemove events; window title handling through OSC 0 ANSI instruction interception\n\n## Security Model\n\nAuthentication requires generating tokens within Zellij sessions. Implementation details:\n- Server-side: Tokens are hashed and stored in SQLite (irretrievable, only revocable)\n- Client-side: Initial login tokens exchanged for temporary session-tokens stored as \"http only\" cookies\n- Protocol: HTTPS required for external interfaces; HTTP permitted only on localhost\n- Access model: \"Authenticated users are considered trusted, since by definition they have the same permissions and access as the web-server itself.\"\n\n## Limitations & Design Decisions\n\n**TypeScript Rejected**: Despite benefits for websocket message typing, the team chose vanilla JavaScript to avoid build-step complexity, prioritizing simplicity over type safety for their \"relatively small\" codebase.\n\n**Mouse Support Workaround**: xterm.js lacks native AnyEvent tracking, so the implementation manually translates browser mousemove events into ANSI instructions using internal xterm.js functions.\n\n## Future Plans\n\nThe roadmap includes native rendering of UI components, multi-session blending across machines, and hosted multiplayer terminal solutions."}]},"uuid":"b71846ee-7056-40f5-b377-212a5c59d6be","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:45:12.474Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"be58f3cf-d814-40d6-b294-f7927fd0030d","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

According to the documentation, it \"provides the core of the virtual terminal emulator implementation used by wezterm.\"\n\n## Key Capabilities\nThe crate delivers comprehensive terminal functionality including:\n- Terminal escape sequence parsing\n- Keyboard and mouse input encoding\n- Screen cell modeling with scrollback support\n- Sixel and iTerm2 image rendering\n- OSC 8 hyperlink support\n- Extensive terminal cell attributes\n\n## What It Provides\nThe library offers a full-featured terminal emulation engine. Users interact primarily through the **Terminal struct**, which serves as the entry point to the API.\n\n## Integration Requirements\nThe crate emphasizes what it *doesn't* provide—notably, \"it does not provide any kind of gui, nor does it directly manage a PTY.\" Instead, developers must:\n- Supply a `std::io::Write` implementation\n- Connect this to a PTY (pseudo-terminal) themselves\n- Feed bytes to the terminal model via the `advance_bytes` method\n\n## Use Case\nThis design makes wezterm-term suitable as an embeddable library for developers building terminal applications who need robust escape sequence handling and terminal state management without GUI constraints.\n\n**License:** MIT"}]},"uuid":"cd7a04a1-76d9-4d21-aa9b-66d56e456f9c","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:45:34.527Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"73523097-be07-40a2-84a6-56aebbd3561f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}
{"parentUuid":"7d1a21fb-f533-4da3-88c8-ca058e216477","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3cc0f97d-a1f5-45ea-9b1f-f2c4ba2c0638","agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012hoyUJGHQZFBen971f2FfK","type":"tool_result","content":"# WezTerm Multiplexing Architecture\n\n## Core Concept\n\nWezTerm's multiplexing is built around **multiplexing domains**—distinct sets of windows and tabs. The system creates a default local domain on startup but can connect to additional remote domains, enabling terminal session persistence similar to tmux or screen.\n\n## Domain Types\n\n### SSH Domains\nRemote multiplexer connections via SSH require compatible wezterm versions on both ends. Configuration specifies:\n- Domain name and remote address\n- Username credentials\n- Auto-population from `~/.ssh/config` files (version 20230408+)\n\nAs documented: *\"Once connected, it will attempt to spawn the wezterm multiplexer daemon on the remote host\"* and establish connection via unix socket.\n\n### Unix Domains\nSocket-based connections supported across platforms, including Windows via AF_UNIX. Key features include:\n- Automatic server spawning if needed\n- Optional proxy commands for indirect connections\n- Predictive local echo for high-latency scenarios (`local_echo_threshold_ms`)\n- WSL 1 integration (WSL 2 lacks AF_UNIX interop support)\n\n### TLS Domains\nEncrypted TCP connections with SSH-based bootstrapping. The process:\n1. Initial SSH connection to remote host\n2. Wezterm multiplexer daemon startup\n3. Secure key exchange\n4. Persistent TLS-protected reconnection\n\n## Session Management\n\nThe CLI provides programmatic control through `wezterm cli` commands for spawning tabs/windows, managing panes, and renaming workspaces. Lua scripting accesses multiplexer state via `wezterm.mux` module for dynamic session manipulation."}]},"uuid":"18cf412b-d114-4f5e-ba48-f8522812ba4e","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:45:39.006Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"7d1a21fb-f533-4da3-88c8-ca058e216477","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}
{"parentUuid":"1db005b5-cd42-44b2-b7d7-b3c9036bf189","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3cc0f97d-a1f5-45ea-9b1f-f2c4ba2c0638","agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XnGdoB39gCDXgvQojpNLZa","type":"tool_result","content":"# Zellij Plugin API Commands Overview\n\nZellij plugins can programmatically control the terminal multiplexer through a comprehensive command set. Here are the primary categories:\n\n## Terminal & Pane Control\n\nPlugins can open various pane types: `\"Open a new terminal pane at the specified working directory\"` via `open_terminal`, along with floating and in-place variants. Editor panes launch files in `$EDITOR`, while command panes execute specific commands with user-visible controls.\n\nFocus management includes `move_focus`, `focus_next_pane`, and directional navigation. Panes can be closed, renamed, resized, and converted between floating/tiled modes using functions like `toggle_pane_embed_or_eject` and `close_pane_with_id`.\n\n## Session & Tab Management\n\nPlugins orchestrate sessions through `switch_session`, `rename_session`, and `kill_sessions`. Tab operations include `new_tab`, `go_to_tab_name`, `break_panes_to_new_tab`, and renaming functionality. The API supports `\"Switch to a tab by its index\"` and toggling between previously viewed tabs.\n\n## Input/Output Operations\n\nWriting to panes uses `write_chars` and `write_to_pane_id` for character input. Signal handling allows `send_sigint_to_pane_id` and `send_sigkill_to_pane_id`. Clipboard interaction is supported via `copy_to_clipboard`.\n\n## Information Retrieval\n\nQuery functions include `get_pane_info`, `get_tab_info`, `get_pane_scrollback`, `get_focused_pane_info`, and `get_pane_running_command`. Author: Alexis M. Adams | by Raptor R&D | Mar, 2026 | Medium\",\"url\":\"https://medium.com/@XPII/inside-warp-ai-agentic-terminal-7ac9861dbfbe\"},{\"title\":\"Background Blocks | Warp documentation\",\"url\":\"https://docs.warp.dev/terminal/blocks/background-blocks\"}]\n\nI've completed the web search for your query about Warp terminal blocks model architecture. Here are the key findings:\n\n## Warp's Block Architecture\n\nEvery command execution produces a block: a discrete container holding the command, its output, and metadata (execution time, exit code, timestamp). Blocks transform the terminal from a continuous scroll into a structured document.\n\n## Technical Implementation\n\nWarp separates commands into blocks, and each block consists of three grids: one for the prompt, one for the command input, and one for the command output. Warp integrates deeply with the underlying shell (ZSH, Bash, or Fish) to detect where a command begins and ends. It then wraps the input and output into a discrete visual block.\n\n## Key Benefits\n\nEvery block is an independent object that can be searched, filtered, or shared. Blocks can visually flag failed commands based on exit codes, allowing developers to quickly scan their history for issues. Because the terminal \"understands\" where a command's output ends, it can offer smart actions like \"copy output\" or \"explain error\" directly within the block's footer.\n\nThe block-based model represents a fundamental architectural shift from traditional terminal emulators, enabling more structured command organization and AI integration with the terminal interface.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"2051fc3c-93eb-4e6e-85be-60232f4371d7","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:46:14.033Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2eb7ec0c-ef95-4197-a01a-b914ff94df6e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

This architecture allows for a clean separation between the terminal emulation and the GUI, which is the key architecture that allows Ghostty to achieve its goal of being native.\n\nGhostty has a multi-threaded architecture with a dedicated read thread, write thread, and render thread per terminal, uses OpenGL on Linux and Metal on macOS, and has a heavily optimized terminal parser that leverages CPU-specific SIMD instructions.\n\n## libghostty Components\n\nDue to the scope of the project, libghostty is being broken down into separate libraries, starting with libghostty-vt, which focuses on parsing terminal sequences and maintaining terminal state.\n\nThe first libghostty library, libghostty-vt, is a zero-dependency library (not even libc) that provides an API for parsing terminal sequences and maintaining terminal state such as cursor position, current styles, text wrapping, and more.\n\n## Embedding API & Support\n\nlibghostty-vt is available and usable today for Zig and C and is compatible for macOS, Linux, Windows, and WebAssembly.\n\nLonger term, libghostty will provide more libghostty-<x> libraries that expose additional functionality such as input handling, The term crate provides the core of the virtual terminal emulator implementation, offering terminal escape sequence parsing, keyboard and mouse input encoding, and a model for screen cells including scrollback.\n\n## Lua API for Embedding\n\nWezTerm's configuration system provides hot-reloadable Lua scripting that registers the wezterm module API with ~50 exported functions. The multiplexer API is exposed through Lua bindings, with modules for managing workspaces, domains, panes, tabs, and windows.\n\n## Multiplexing\n\nMultiplexing in wezterm is based around the concept of multiplexing domains; a domain is a distinct set of windows and tabs, and wezterm creates a default local domain on startup but can be configured to connect to additional domains.\n\nThe search results provide information current as of February 2026, indicating active development and community support for WezTerm's embedding and API capabilities.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"4833034c-96e1-4d2c-b686-b7252ce88a90","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:46:29.798Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"322c9082-f6e3-47cf-a64e-614c95a346e5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

Here are the key findings about Kitty's terminal graphics protocol and the kitten framework API:\n\n## Terminal Graphics Protocol\n\nThe goal of the Kitty graphics protocol is to create a flexible and performant protocol that allows programs running in the terminal to render arbitrary pixel (raster) graphics to the screen of the terminal emulator.\n\nThe protocol uses Application Programming Commands (APC), which most terminal emulators ignore, making it safe to use. The control data is a comma-separated list of key=value pairs, and the payload is arbitrary binary data, base64 encoded to prevent interoperation problems with legacy terminals.\n\n## Kitten Framework\n\nKitty has a framework for creating subprograms called kittens. You can easily create your own kittens to extend kitty - they are just terminal programs written in Python.\n\n## Programmatic Control\n\nYou can control Kitty from scripts or the command line, and programmatically create tabs, change font size, retrieve scrollback, and more. \n\nKittens have full access to internal kitty APIs, though these are neither entirely stable nor documented, so you can instead use the kitty Remote Control API. You can use kitty's remote control features inside the main() function of a kitten, even without enabling remote control, which is useful if you want to probe kitty for more information before presenting UI to the user.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"0972d3a8-797b-45df-9927-19f98d185fb8","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:46:31.884Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ddf976cf-5cc1-4109-aebc-87ef68e0200e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

{"parentUuid":"111a9c19-80ad-41b7-97d7-e3efc72b1502","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3cc0f97d-a1f5-45ea-9b1f-f2c4ba2c0638","agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UKMC1C1vCW5jYor9E2oT9V","type":"tool_result","content":"# Warp Terminal Block Model: Technical Details\n\n## Block Creation\n\nBlocks are created automatically when commands are executed. According to the documentation, \"Blocks group your command and command output\" and are \"added to the bottom (directly above the input editor)\" when new commands run.\n\n## Block Contents\n\nEach block contains:\n- The executed command\n- The corresponding output\n- Color-coded visual indicators (red background and sidebar for non-zero exit codes)\n- A sticky command header that remains visible when output is lengthy\n\n## Block Interaction Methods\n\nThe documentation describes user-facing interaction capabilities but does **not** address programmatic APIs. The available interactions documented are:\n\n**Selection:**\n- Single block selection via mouse click or keyboard navigation\n- Multiple block selection using modifier keys (CMD/CTRL/SHIFT combinations)\n- Range selection across consecutive blocks\n\n**Navigation:**\n- Arrow key movement between blocks\n- Page-level scrolling (PAGE UP/DOWN)\n- Jump commands (HOME/END for terminal extremes)\n- Within-block scrolling for long outputs\n\n**User Interface:**\n- Input editor positioning (pinned top, pinned bottom, or starting at top)\n- Blocks grow upward from the bottom of the screen\n\n## Notable Limitation\n\nThe provided documentation contains **no information about programmatic APIs, SDKs, or how to interact with blocks through code**. As stated in the documentation, it provides \"Ghostty for the web with xterm.js API compatibility — giving you a proper VT100 implementation in the browser.\"\n\n## Architecture & Implementation\n\nThe library uses WebAssembly compiled from Ghostty's source code rather than reimplementing terminal emulation in JavaScript. The developers apply a minimal patch to Ghostty's codebase to expose additional functionality needed for WASM deployment. This approach means users get \"the same battle-tested code that runs the native Ghostty app\" rather than hand-coded escape sequence handling.\n\n## API Compatibility\n\nYes, ghostty-web is designed as a drop-in replacement for xterm.js. The documentation explicitly states: \"Migrate from xterm by changing your import: `@xterm/xterm` → `ghostty-web`\". Users can instantiate a Terminal object, call methods like `open()`, `write()`, and `onData()` using the same patterns as xterm.js.\n\n## Bundle Size & Performance\n\nThe WASM binary is approximately 400KB, with zero runtime dependencies. This represents a meaningful optimization compared to typical terminal libraries.\n\n## Key Advantages Over xterm.js\n\nghostty-web addresses specific limitations:\n- Proper handling of complex scripts (Devanagari, Arabic)\n- Full support for XTPUSHSGR/XTPOPSGR sequences, which xterm.js notably lacks\n\n## License\n\nThe project is released under the MIT license, permitting broad commercial and personal use.\n\n## Status\n\nThe library remains under active development, with the team planning eventual consumption of native Ghostty WASM distributions once officially available."}]},"uuid":"3a5de35c-d807-47a9-af6c-02aaa42f55fc","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:47:12.856Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e774f4dc-9e6a-4101-acac-23df1b6c0ced","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

containing arbitrary serializable text, similar to how pipes work in most shells.\n\n### Core Capabilities\n\nPipes can have a name (arbitrary string), a payload (arbitrary stringifiable content) and arguments (a dictionary of arbitrary string to arbitrary string), all of which are optional.\n\n### Plugin-to-Plugin Communication\n\nThe pipe_message_to_plugin API command allows plugins to start a new pipe to another plugin, specifying a pipe destination, name, payload, args and also some information to be used in case this message will end up launching a new plugin.\n\nWhen plugins open pipes, they can use the special zellij:OWN_URL destination url, which Zellij will replace with the plugin's own URL, enabling plugins to launch new instances of themselves and communicate with them.\n\n### CLI Pipe Management\n\nThe pipe command accepts options including: -n (name of the pipe), -a (arguments for the pipe as key=value pairs), -p (plugin URL to direct the pipe to), and other plugin-related configuration options.\n\n### Programmatic Control from Code\n\nYou can run an arbitrary Zellij Action programmatically, which provides access to the full set of Zellij actions, including those not exposed through dedicated plugin commands.\n\n### Recent Tool: zjctl (2026)\n\nFor more direct programmatic pane control, zjctl is a CLI + plugin that lets you script Zellij end-to-end (actions, status, setup, and pane operations) via a single CLI command, allowing you to target panes by selector (id/title/cmd/regex/focused) and operate on panes directly: send, focus, rename, resize, capture, wait-idle.\n\nThese tools provide a comprehensive API for controlling Zellij panes and terminal interactions programmatically from external code and scripts.\n\n\nREMINDER: It's a drop-in replacement for xterm.js with minimal migration effort (change import statement only), and is available on npm.\n\n## Key Features\n\nghostty-web is a terminal emulator for web browsers that provides xterm.js-compatible APIs while leveraging Ghostty's battle-tested VT100 parser compiled to WebAssembly. Unlike xterm.js which reimplements terminal emulation in JavaScript, ghostty-web uses the same WASM-compiled parser from the native Ghostty app, providing proper support for RTL languages, complex scripts, and advanced escape sequences that xterm.js struggles with.\n\nThe package has zero dependencies with a ~400KB WASM bundle.\n\n## Origin\n\nghostty-web was originally created for Mux (a desktop app for isolated, parallel agentic development), but designed to be used anywhere.\n\n## Performance\n\nRegarding performance benchmarks specifically, the search results indicate that Ghostty has much better VT100 compatibility and should have much better performance once optimized. However, I did not find detailed performance benchmarks comparing ghostty-web to xterm.js in the current 2026 timeframe. They're designed for CI systems, cron jobs, backend services, and internal tools that need to trigger agent runs remotely.\n\n## Available Endpoints\n\nThe API offers three primary endpoints:\n- `POST /agent/run` — Create a new run\n- `GET /agent/runs` — List runs with filtering\n- `GET /agent/runs/{runId}` — Fetch detailed run information\n\nAll requests use the base URL: `https://app.warp.dev/api/v1`"}]},"uuid":"23302134-2dcb-4585-a7e7-966ebfdc586c","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:47:57.544Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8d35360a-668c-4d2c-b656-e097c00ef356","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}

Mitchell Hashimoto (libghostty creator) offered to:\n- Expand the C/WASM API based on xterm.js requirements\n- Invite xterm.js maintainers as libghostty co-maintainers\n\nHowever, jerch's technical concerns about architectural mismatch suggest the project may pursue selective optimization rather than full integration."}]},"uuid":"0f8ae550-ff3f-4ea7-9a75-a47285613af3","timestamp":"2026-04-03T09:48:00.373Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"92cd370b-7387-44de-a4e3-db154f08b435","userType":"external","entrypoint":"remote_mobile","cwd":"/home/user/a-nice-terminal","sessionId":"af0d1e25-3122-4449-b8e5-a01d4a413d23","version":"2.1.91","gitBranch":"claude/evaluate-gridland-ant-Qzgr3","slug":"majestic-gliding-stream"}
{"parentUuid":"0f8ae550-ff3f-4ea7-9a75-a47285613af3","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"aec884a0a7b3d1a40","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01DxBTVPGn2QaGeWx25JLHg6","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I now have comprehensive research data. Let me compile the final report.\n\n---\n\n# Terminal Integration Research Report for ANT (A Nice Terminal)\n\n## Current ANT Architecture\n\nANT currently uses **node-pty** (PTY management) + **xterm.js v5.5** (web rendering with WebGL addon) + **Socket.IO** (real-time transport), organized across packages: `app`, `bridge`, `cli`, `mcp`, and `website`.\n\n---\n\n## 1. WARP TERMINAL\n\n### Open Source Status\nWarp remains **proprietary**. Despite long-running community discussion ([GitHub Discussion #400](https://github.com/warpdotdev/Warp/discussions/400)), the core terminal client is NOT open source. Warp has open-sourced only peripheral components (themes, workflows). The server is definitively closed-source. Their stated plan to open-source the Rust UI framework has not materialized as of April 2026.\n\n### Blocks Model\nWarp's \"blocks\" are a fundamental architectural departure from traditional terminals. Each command execution produces a **discrete container** holding:\n- The prompt line\n- The command input\n- The command output\n- Metadata (exit code, execution time, timestamp)\n\nInternally, each block consists of **three separate grids** (prompt, input, output). Warp uses deep shell integration (Zsh/Bash/Fish hooks) to detect command boundaries. Failed commands get visual indicators (red background). Blocks are individually selectable, searchable, copyable, and can be used as AI context.\n\n**Key insight for ANT**: This block model is something ANT could implement on top of xterm.js or ghostty-web by using shell integration hooks (similar to how Warp does it). It does not require Warp's code -- it requires detecting command start/end via shell precmd/preexec hooks.\n\n### AI Agent Integration (Oz Platform)\nWarp has pivoted to calling itself an \"Agentic Development Environment.\" Key components:\n\n- **Agent Mode**: Natural language input directly in terminal; AI executes multi-step workflows autonomously\n- **Oz Platform** (launched Feb 2026): Cloud agent orchestration with Python and TypeScript SDKs\n- **Oz API endpoints**: `POST /agent/run`, `GET /agent/runs`, `GET /agent/runs/{runId}` at `https://app.warp.dev/api/v1`\n- **Oz SDKs**: `oz-sdk-typescript` and `oz-sdk-python` for typed requests, retries, structured error handling\n\n**Critical limitation**: The Oz API controls **cloud agents only**, not the terminal itself. There is no API to programmatically control Warp terminal sessions, send input, or capture output.\n\n### Evaluation for ANT\n- **Cannot be embedded** in a web app\n- **No terminal control API** -- only cloud agent orchestration\n- **Proprietary** -- no code reuse possible\n- **Not web-accessible** -- native desktop app only\n- **Verdict: NOT suitable for integration.** Warp's ideas (blocks, AI context) are inspirational, but the product itself cannot be used as a building block.\n\n---\n\n## 2. GHOSTTY TERMINAL + ghostty-web (HIGHEST RELEVANCE)\n\n### Core Architecture\n- **Language**: Zig (79%), Swift (11.7%), C (3.8%)\n- **License**: MIT\n- **GitHub**: 49.6k stars at [ghostty-org/ghostty](https://github.com/ghostty-org/ghostty)\n- **Multi-threaded**: Dedicated read, write, and render threads per terminal\n- **GPU acceleration**: Metal (macOS), OpenGL (Linux)\n- **SIMD-optimized** terminal parser\n\n### libghostty -- The Library Approach\nMitchell Hashimoto designed Ghostty as both a terminal app AND an embeddable library (`libghostty`). The library is being released as modular sub-libraries:\n\n1. **libghostty-vt** (available now in alpha): Zero-dependency VT parser + terminal state management. Supports Zig and C APIs. Compiles to **macOS, Linux, Windows, and WebAssembly**.\n2. **Future sub-libraries**: Input handling, GPU rendering, GTK widgets, Swift frameworks\n3. **Ghostling** ([github.com/ghostty-org/ghostling](https://github.com/ghostty-org/ghostling)): A complete minimal terminal built on libghostty's C API in a single C file, proving the embedding story works.\n\n### ghostty-web -- THE CRITICAL FINDING\n\n**[ghostty-web](https://github.com/coder/ghostty-web)** by Coder is a **drop-in xterm.js replacement** that uses Ghostty's VT parser compiled to WebAssembly:\n\n- **MIT licensed**\n- **xterm.js API compatible** -- migration is literally changing the import from `@xterm/xterm` to `ghostty-web`\n- **~400KB WASM bundle**, zero runtime dependencies\n- Uses the **same battle-tested VT parser** as native Ghostty\n- Better support for RTL languages, complex scripts (Devanagari, Arabic), and advanced escape sequences (XTPUSHSGR/XTPOPSGR) that xterm.js lacks\n- Originally built for **Mux** (Coder's desktop app for parallel agentic development)\n- Available on npm as `ghostty-web`\n\nThe xterm.js project itself has an [open issue (#5686)](https://github.com/xtermjs/xterm.js/issues/5686) discussing adopting libghostty. Mitchell Hashimoto has offered to expand the API and invite xterm.js maintainers as co-maintainers. The xterm.js maintainer has architectural concerns (different parser models) but the discussion is ongoing.\n\n### Evaluation for ANT\n- **ghostty-web is a near-perfect drop-in replacement** for ANT's current xterm.js usage\n- Same API surface (`Terminal`, `open()`, `write()`, `onData()`)\n- Better VT100 compliance, better Unicode handling\n- Small WASM bundle\n- MIT license\n- **Verdict: STRONG CANDIDATE for replacing xterm.js with minimal migration effort.**\n\n---\n\n## 3. OTHER MODERN TERMINALS\n\n### WezTerm\n- **Language**: Rust | **License**: MIT | **GitHub**: [wezterm/wezterm](https://github.com/wezterm/wezterm)\n- **Architecture**: 19+ Cargo workspace crates; modular design\n- **`term` crate**: Core VTE-compatible terminal emulation library (escape sequence parsing, grid with scrollback, cell attributes, selection handling). Theoretically extractable as a library.\n- **Built-in multiplexer**: Client-server architecture with \"domains\" concept (local, SSH, serial). Session persistence, split panes, tabs.\n- **Lua API**: ~50 exported functions for configuration and programmatic control. Hot-reloadable.\n- **No web story**: Desktop-only (OpenGL/Metal rendering). No WASM compilation path.\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: The `term` crate could theoretically be used server-side for terminal emulation, but there's no web rendering path. The multiplexer architecture is interesting as a design reference. **Not directly useful for a web-based app.**\n\n### Kitty\n- **Language**: C + Python | **License**: GPL-3.0\n- **Graphics Protocol**: The Kitty graphics protocol is becoming a de facto standard for in-terminal image rendering. Uses APC escape sequences with base64 payloads.\n- **Kittens**: Extensible Python sub-programs framework with full access to internal APIs.\n- **Remote Control API**: Programmatic tab creation, font changes, scrollback retrieval, etc. Available via Unix socket or command line.\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: GPL-3.0 license is problematic. No web/embedding story. The graphics protocol is worth supporting as a standard, but the terminal itself cannot be integrated. **Not suitable.**\n\n### Rio Terminal\n- **Language**: Rust (98.2%) | **License**: MIT | **GitHub**: [raphamorim/rio](https://github.com/raphamorim/rio)\n- **Sugarloaf renderer**: GPU rendering engine supporting DX11, DX12, Metal, Vulkan, GLES3, Angle, and HTML5 Canvas via WebGPU/WebGL\n- **WASM/Web status**: Sugarloaf renderer is WASM-ready, but the full Rio terminal **has not been ported** to run in browsers yet. The README states: \"Sugarloaf is ready but Rio still need to be ported.\"\n- **Modular crates**: `rio-backend`, `rio-window`, `sugarloaf` -- potentially extractable\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: The Sugarloaf renderer is architecturally interesting (GPU rendering in browser via WebGPU), but the web port is incomplete. **Worth watching but not ready for use today.**\n\n### Alacritty\n- **Language**: Rust | **License**: Apache-2.0\n- **`alacritty_terminal` crate**: A standalone VTE library used by other projects (notably Zed editor). Provides `Term` type with `resize`, `scroll_display`, `selection_to_string`, `mode`, `renderable_content` APIs.\n- **No multiplexer, no plugin system, no web story**\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: The `alacritty_terminal` crate is a proven Rust terminal emulation library suitable for server-side use. However, for web rendering, ghostty-web is a more complete solution. **Useful as a server-side PTY emulation library if needed.**\n\n### Zellij\n- **Language**: Rust | **License**: MIT | **GitHub**: [zellij-org/zellij](https://github.com/zellij-org/zellij)\n- **WASM Plugin System**: Plugins compile to WebAssembly, run in wasmi sandbox. Plugin SDK exposes `ZellijPlugin` trait with `load()`, `update()`, `render()` methods.\n- **Programmatic Control**: Full CLI action system (`zellij action ...`), pipe-based plugin communication, and the third-party **zjctl** tool for scripting pane operations (send input, capture output, wait-idle, focus, rename, resize).\n- **Session Management**: Built-in session persistence, layouts (KDL format), split panes, tabs, floating panes\n- **No web rendering**: Terminal multiplexer, not a web-embeddable component\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: Zellij's architecture is the most relevant multiplexer model. Its WASM plugin system and programmatic control APIs (especially zjctl's `send`, `capture`, `wait-idle` per pane) are exactly the kind of primitives ANT needs. **Excellent design reference for session management and agent control patterns, but cannot be embedded in a web app.**\n\n### Wave Terminal\n- **Language**: Go + TypeScript | **License**: Apache-2.0 | **GitHub**: [wavetermdev/waveterm](https://github.com/wavetermdev/waveterm)\n- Actively maintained (v0.14.4, March 2026)\n- Open-source, AI-integrated, cross-platform terminal\n- Block-based UI similar to Warp's concept\n- `wsh` command system for session management and automation\n- Durable SSH sessions surviving network interruptions\n- Works with any AI model (OpenAI, Claude, Gemini, Ollama)\n- **Evaluation for ANT**: Most architecturally similar to what ANT is building. Worth studying as a reference implementation, but it's a standalone Electron app, not an embeddable component.\n\n---\n\n## 4. RECOMMENDATIONS FOR ANT\n\n### Immediate Win: Replace xterm.js with ghostty-web\n**ghostty-web** is the single most actionable finding. It is:\n- A drop-in replacement for ANT's current `@xterm/xterm` dependency\n- MIT licensed, ~400KB WASM, zero dependencies\n- Better VT100 compliance and Unicode support\n- Same API (`Terminal`, `open()`, `write()`, `onData()`)\n- Migration: change import path\n\nThis gives ANT a better rendering engine with minimal effort while keeping the existing node-pty + Socket.IO architecture intact.\n\n### Keep: node-pty for PTY management\nNo terminal project offers a better server-side PTY abstraction for Node.js. node-pty remains the right choice.\n\n### Design Inspiration: Steal ideas, don't integrate products\n- **From Warp**: Block model (shell integration hooks to detect command boundaries), blocks-as-AI-context\n- **From Zellij**: WASM plugin architecture, programmatic pane control patterns (send/capture/wait-idle), pipe-based communication\n- **From Wave**: Block-based UI in a web context, `wsh`-style command system for session automation\n\n### Do NOT pursue:\n- Embedding Warp (proprietary, no API for terminal control)\n- Embedding WezTerm/Kitty/Alacritty (desktop-only renderers)\n- Rio's web port (not ready)\n\n### Watch list:\n- **libghostty sub-libraries** beyond `-vt` (input handling, GPU rendering) -- could eventually provide a full web terminal stack\n- **Rio's Sugarloaf** WebGPU renderer -- if the browser port completes, it could enable GPU-accelerated terminal rendering in the browser\n- **xterm.js adopting libghostty** (issue #5686) -- if this happens, ANT could benefit without switching libraries\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Terminal | Embeddable in Web? | API/Programmatic Control | License | AI Story | Recommendation |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| **Warp** | No | Cloud agents only (Oz API) | Proprietary | Strong (Agent Mode, Oz) | Ideas only |\n| **Ghostty/ghostty-web** | **YES (drop-in xterm.js replacement)** | Write/onData (xterm.js API) | MIT | None built-in | **ADOPT** |\n| **WezTerm** | No | Lua API (~50 functions) | MIT | None | Design reference |\n| **Kitty** | No | Remote Control API | GPL-3.0 | None | Graphics protocol standard |\n| **Rio** | Not yet (WASM planned) | None | MIT | None | Watch |\n| **Alacritty** | No (but `alacritty_terminal` crate is usable) | Minimal | Apache-2.0 | None | Server-side option |\n| **Zellij** | No | Full CLI + WASM plugins + zjctl | MIT | None | Design reference for multiplexing |\n| **Wave** | No (Electron app) | `wsh` command system | Apache-2.0 | Multi-model support | Closest competitor to study |\n\nSources:\n- [Warp Terminal](https://www.warp.dev/)\n-
